  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1842e691-b33a-45d5-9233-a9380fd024a0'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14003571691091433455">It's 1917, and World War I is at its zenith when Hazel and James first catch sight of each other at a London party. She's a shy and talented pianist; he's a newly minted soldier with dreams of becoming an architect. When they fall in love, it's immediate and deep--and cut short when James is shipped off to the killing fields.<br/><br/>Aubrey Edwards is also headed toward the trenche</span>
  <span id="freeText14003571691091433455" style="display:none">It's 1917, and World War I is at its zenith when Hazel and James first catch sight of each other at a London party. She's a shy and talented pianist; he's a newly minted soldier with dreams of becoming an architect. When they fall in love, it's immediate and deep--and cut short when James is shipped off to the killing fields.<br /><br />Aubrey Edwards is also headed toward the trenches. A gifted musician who's played Carnegie Hall, he's a member of the 15th New York Infantry, an all-African-American regiment being sent to Europe to help end the Great War. Love is the last thing on his mind. But that's before he meets Colette Fournier, a Belgian chanteuse who's already survived unspeakable tragedy at the hands of the Germans.<br /><br />Thirty years after these four lovers' fates collide, the Greek goddess Aphrodite tells their stories to her husband, Hephaestus, and her lover, Ares, in a luxe Manhattan hotel room at the height of World War II. She seeks to answer the age-old question: Why are Love and War eternally drawn to one another? But her quest for a conclusion that will satisfy her jealous husband uncovers a multi-threaded tale of prejudice, trauma, and music and reveals that War is no match for the power of Love.<br /><br /><b>A sweeping, multi-layered romance with a divine twist, by the Printz Honor-winning author of <i>The Passion of Dolssa</i>, set in the perilous days of World Wars I and II.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14003571691091433455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1518946-is-this-desirable-to-teens-i-know-it-is">Is this desirable to teens? I know it is designated as for ages 12 and up, but will my teen patrons really want to take it out and &quot;get it&quot;? Thank you</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1518946'><a id="like_count_community_question_1518946" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1518946?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">10 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F44107480-lovely-war">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/85392795-emma-the-bookworm"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1534275727i/85392795._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/85392795-emma-the-bookworm">Emma_the_bookworm</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">As a 14 year old, I really enjoyed this book! I didn't think that the romance was too much, and it definitely felt age appropriate. The writing style <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">As a 14 year old, I really enjoyed this book! I didn't think that the romance was too much, and it definitely felt age appropriate. The writing style and the plot were easy for me to follow, and I never felt that the book was overly complicated or dense.<br /><br />One of my favorite parts of Lovely War was that Greek Gods were tied into the story. I was only familiar with Greek gods from reading Percy Jackson, so it was fun to read about them again in a new setting, with different personalities then I was used to. I also loved that music played such a huge role in Lovely War, and that I got to read about the beginnings of jazz in the US. <br /><br />The hardest part of this book for me was reading about the pain and suffering that comes with war, but I thought the author handled it very well. The book is not overly depressing, violent or graphic. However, there are some descriptions of life in the trenches, racial prejudice/hate crimes and PTSD. There is also discussion about racial prejudice in the military. I think that it would be a great way to start/continue a conversation about racial prejudice in the US, especially because one of the main characters is an African American soldier facing discrimination.<br /><br />Lovely War had a very creative plot, with characters who I connected with and cared about. I would recommend this to any teenager who likes historical fiction, enjoys romance that isn't graphic, and appreciates music. I hope this helps! :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3062308276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9841667018321932314">I cried at least 7 separate times while reading this book. The four central characters are all endearing and lovely, and I was deeply touched by the humanity and hope that leaked during a tragic period of history, and the relationship between love and war. Huge props to Berry for incorporating the perspectives of black soldiers with such care and poignancy while giving Aubrey so much personality. While the romance does develop quickly, I still found the book to be charming and heart-wrenching gi</span>
  <span id="freeText9841667018321932314" style="display:none">I cried at least 7 separate times while reading this book. The four central characters are all endearing and lovely, and I was deeply touched by the humanity and hope that leaked during a tragic period of history, and the relationship between love and war. Huge props to Berry for incorporating the perspectives of black soldiers with such care and poignancy while giving Aubrey so much personality. While the romance does develop quickly, I still found the book to be charming and heart-wrenching given the circumstances that these couples have gone through. If you're not into romance, you might not like it, but if you're a romantic sucker at heart, you'll probably cry with me too lol.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2593339392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6683219467373461233">I love this book desperately. I did write it, so the possibility of bias is real. :) I can't wait to share it with the world. The year-plus I spent researching, writing, and revising it was intense, and harrowing at times, but I'm thrilled with where we landed. Here's hoping you enjoy it, too. <br/><br/>Hazel, a pianist, and James, a builder-turned-soldier, meet at a London dance in late 1917, on the eve of his departure for the trenches of World War I. Aubrey, a Harlem ragtime musician, and Colette, a Be</span>
  <span id="freeText6683219467373461233" style="display:none">I love this book desperately. I did write it, so the possibility of bias is real. :) I can't wait to share it with the world. The year-plus I spent researching, writing, and revising it was intense, and harrowing at times, but I'm thrilled with where we landed. Here's hoping you enjoy it, too. <br /><br />Hazel, a pianist, and James, a builder-turned-soldier, meet at a London dance in late 1917, on the eve of his departure for the trenches of World War I. Aubrey, a Harlem ragtime musician, and Colette, a Belgian refugee who has lost everything to the war, meet in a YMCA relief hut at the American training base at Saint-Nazaire, France. <br /><br />Aphrodite and Ares meet for a secret tryst in a Manhattan hotel room, only to be caught and exposed by Hephaestus, the goddess of love's jealous husband. Aphrodite, as the defendant in a mock courtroom trial, spins the intertwined stories of both pairs of star-crossed lovers in a plea to soften her husband's anger. With additional testimony from Ares (war), and ultimately, Apollo (art) and Hades (death), the gods' stories explore how far hope can reach into the abyss of wartime destruction and despair, and whether, in a broken world, there's still a case to be made for love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6683219467373461233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13355153681612610283">im surprised i broke my WWI/WWII historical fiction hiatus, but i kept seeing so many positive reviews for this, so i made an exception.<br/><br/>and i understand the hype. its quite something to write such a lovely story about war - you wouldnt think its possible. and this is, lovely. but at the heart of it, it just feels like every other WW story. <br/><br/>the only novelty of this is that its told from perspective of greek gods and i love that. i found this part of the story the most interesting, so im bummed th</span>
  <span id="freeText13355153681612610283" style="display:none">im surprised i broke my WWI/WWII historical fiction hiatus, but i kept seeing so many positive reviews for this, so i made an exception.<br /><br />and i understand the hype. its quite something to write such a lovely story about war - you wouldnt think its possible. and this is, lovely. but at the heart of it, it just feels like every other WW story. <br /><br />the only novelty of this is that its told from perspective of greek gods and i love that. i found this part of the story the most interesting, so im bummed that there wasnt more than just the set up, the conclusion, and only a couple of interjections - it just wasnt enough for me. <br /><br />but regardless, this is your classic war story about hope, resilience, and love.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2794767046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794767046" />
    <a title="sarah xoxo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57354360-sarah-xoxo"><img alt="sarah xoxo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567765387p2/57354360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2794767046?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sarah xoxo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sarah xoxo" href="/user/show/57354360-sarah-xoxo">sarah xoxo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=all-time-favs">all-time-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57354360-sarah-xoxo?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794767046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1537624995927150900"><i>I'm in love</i><br/><br/>This book is narrated by greek gods, but are we sure it isn't written by one too? Lovely War feels as if it is on a plane higher than us mere mortals. Julie Berry, I'm not sure what magic you cast over me but please never stop. <br/><br/>It usually takes me around 50 pages or so to get acquainted with a story, the characters and setting. With Lovely War, I was entranced from page one. By page ten I was laughing. By page fifteen I was swooning. By page twenty, I felt as if I knew these character</span>
  <span id="freeText1537624995927150900" style="display:none"><i>I'm in love</i><br /><br />This book is narrated by greek gods, but are we sure it isn't written by one too? Lovely War feels as if it is on a plane higher than us mere mortals. Julie Berry, I'm not sure what magic you cast over me but please never stop. <br /><br />It usually takes me around 50 pages or so to get acquainted with a story, the characters and setting. With Lovely War, I was entranced from page one. By page ten I was laughing. By page fifteen I was swooning. By page twenty, I felt as if I knew these characters, their souls. <br /><br />I cannot properly articulate the beauty, the despair, the magic of this book. Nothing I could ever write about it would do it justice. <br /><br /><i>“Let them start their dreadful wars, let destruction rain down, and let plague sweep through, but I will still be here, doing my work, holding humankind together with love like this.” </i><br /><br />What initially transfixed me was the writing. Julie Berry's prose speaks to me on a spiritual level. I adored the god's narration. It made this seemingly common and overdone story suddenly feel new and, well, <i>lovely.</i> What kept me reading were the characters. They felt real, raw and perfectly flawed. They were endearing and charming and every other synonym. <br /><br />This book deserves five stars through and through simply for the emotions it evoked in me. In a mere sentence it had me tearing up, in another it had me closing the book and simply whispering 'no no no no no.' <br /><br /><i>“I envy your mortals."<br />“As Ares says, they die, you know.”<br />“They do. But the lucky ones live first."</i><br /><br />Lovely War was such a personal experience for me that is impossible for me to think about it in a purely objective sense. It without a doubt has earned its place on my list of All Time Favourites. <br /><br />read this. experience the beauty. taste the sadness. feel the love.<i> you won't regret it. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1537624995927150900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3249964277" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14000090895433063921">This book took me on a journey. Oof.<br/><br/>If you're looking for a historical fiction with outstandingly beautiful prose that you'll want to highlight and bookmark endlessly and some fantastical elements in the forms of gods and goddesses watching over mortals at war, then you have to read Lovely War, following four different characters, from different walks of life as their worlds converge during WWI.<br/><br/>I absolutely loved how this book was written from the perspective of Aphrodite, Hades, Ares, and Apoll</span>
  <span id="freeText14000090895433063921" style="display:none">This book took me on a journey. Oof.<br /><br />If you're looking for a historical fiction with outstandingly beautiful prose that you'll want to highlight and bookmark endlessly and some fantastical elements in the forms of gods and goddesses watching over mortals at war, then you have to read Lovely War, following four different characters, from different walks of life as their worlds converge during WWI.<br /><br />I absolutely loved how this book was written from the perspective of Aphrodite, Hades, Ares, and Apollo. Each of their voices was so distinct, and seeing their direct involvement in these mortals' lives was so fascinating to read. I'm a sucker for any retelling that includes the Greek gods, so this was the book of my dreams in it being a historical fiction mixed together with Greek mythology. <br /><br />While I do have to say the book dragged on a little for me and the descriptions of the battles themselves were dry, this book and the characters within it stole my heart, left me wondering what was going to happen next, and made me fall head over heels for Julie Berry's gorgeous prose. I highly implore any historical fiction lover to pick up this book because the prose itself is something that needs to be admired.<br /><br />AT A GLANCE<br />- Gods and goddesses tell each other about an epic love story set during WWI<br />- War, heartbreak, romance, everything you need to have a gorgeously written story<br />- The prettiest prose in any historical fiction I've ever read<br /><br />CONTENT WARNINGS: Blackface (condemned in the story), racism, lynching, PTSD, war</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3147893836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12069282232863760814">This book would have maybe gotten four stars because of the discussion of topics such as James Reese Europe and the introduction of jazz in Europe during WWI, the treatment of black troops during the war, and the horrors of the trenches. And yet, the framing technique of a story told by Ares, Aphrodite and Hephaestus did absolutely not work for me. The writing was ok, if sappy when the narrative concentrated on Hazel, James, Colette and Aubrey but it was stilted and awkward when the gods were sp</span>
  <span id="freeText12069282232863760814" style="display:none">This book would have maybe gotten four stars because of the discussion of topics such as James Reese Europe and the introduction of jazz in Europe during WWI, the treatment of black troops during the war, and the horrors of the trenches. And yet, the framing technique of a story told by Ares, Aphrodite and Hephaestus did absolutely not work for me. The writing was ok, if sappy when the narrative concentrated on Hazel, James, Colette and Aubrey but it was stilted and awkward when the gods were speaking amongst themselves. The two intertwined love stories were ok, but very soap-opera inspired with long pauses and dramatic kisses. If that is your kind of thing, then you'll enjoy this. I just found that the story would have been fine without the gods and without the sappiness. I would probably have dropped it down to two stars had there not been the good historical reminders I mentioned above and the Historical Notes and Bibliography not have been included at the end.<br /><br />The plot is framed by what I consider to be a silly scenario in 40s Manhattan where Haphaestus catches Ares and Aphrodite in delecto and in strange rip off of 1001 Nights, Aphrodite recounts a love story set in WWI. Like I said, that whole thing did nothing for me. The adventures of the two couples, Hazel and James (both English) and Colette and Aubrey (Belgian and American respectively) were interesting, if somewhat overdrawn at points. Had the book just focused on the two love stories, I might have enjoyed it more.<br /><br />I nearly forgot to mention that there has been a renewed interest in the music of James Reese Europe, most notably by the American jazz pianist Jason Moran who includes a few songs, including Reveille Blues alluded to in the book, in his live sets and plans an entire album dedicated to the composer/band leader in 2020.<br /><br />I’ll give a more in-depth plot readout later. Just miffed that the top review for this book is one sentence in ALL CAPS and has &gt;520 Likes. I don’t understand how that works.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14125680598078131112"><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/>The <i>Lovely War</i> is truly nothing short of perfect.<br/>I feel a little dim being that I am at something like a loss for words but that is how finishing this book made me feel. I've not read a book in a long time that felt like the most perfect picture of hope and longing and darkness and light.<br/><br/>The <i>Lovely War</i> is a brilliant depiction of historical fiction with a pinch of greek mythology. Aphrodite has been caught in an affair and is demanded an explanation by her husband, Hephaestus. Aphrodite p</span>
  <span id="freeText14125680598078131112" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b><br /><br />The <i>Lovely War</i> is truly nothing short of perfect.<br />I feel a little dim being that I am at something like a loss for words but that is how finishing this book made me feel. I've not read a book in a long time that felt like the most perfect picture of hope and longing and darkness and light.<br /><br />The <i>Lovely War</i> is a brilliant depiction of historical fiction with a pinch of greek mythology. Aphrodite has been caught in an affair and is demanded an explanation by her husband, Hephaestus. Aphrodite presents her case court room style. She then tells the story of Hazel and James, two people who found each other just moments before being ripped apart, and their tale as they struggled to fight their own battles during WWI. Hazel meets Collette and they quickly become best friends, and Hazel watches Collette fall in love with a black soldier, Aubrey, and Aphrodite tells her husband of all their struggles as she pleads her case.<br /><br />I didn't know what to expect going into this. I have a friend or two who has read it and adored it, but I feel like this book truly surprised me. Hazel and James' story starts rather quickly, where as Colette and Aubrey's picks up around the halfway point. The interwoven stories of friendship and love and heartbreak and death and illness are what makes this book perfection.<br /><br />I could not put the book down as I was reading the last 35% of it. It was so fast paced, filled with so much longing and immersive descriptions of the characters surroundings as well as their feelings. I found myself rooting so hard for the two couples to make it through the wartime and end up triumphantly together.<br /><br />As you read, you only dive deeper into each character, becoming more and more in tune with them. As they face hardships, you grow with them. As they fall in love, you fall in love with them.<br /><br />If there was only one thing I could say to review this book, it would be: "READ THIS BOOK"<br /><br />And if my review falls flat, go read all the other raving reviews. You know what, skip the reviews and just <b>
  <i>read the book</i>
</b>. It will not disappoint.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>***also, PLEASE someone hire the director &amp; team who did the Netflix adaptation of The Guernsey Literary and Potato Peel Pie Society and MAKE THIS INTO A MOVIE. Can you imagine that brilliance!? It MUST happen."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_3333803795" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3333803795" />
    <a title="Bkwmlee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45796209-bkwmlee"><img alt="Bkwmlee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493302691p2/45796209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3333803795?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bkwmlee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bkwmlee" href="/user/show/45796209-bkwmlee">Bkwmlee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780147512970" href="/book/show/53081194-lovely-war">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45796209-bkwmlee?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45796209-bkwmlee?shelf=book-club-botm">book-club-botm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3333803795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11645018807614699471">This was a delightful read, one that I was a bit apprehensive going into it, but ended up really enjoying! The premise of the story is a unique one: two young couples — Hazel and James, Colette and Aubrey — fall in love amongst the turbulence of World War I, their story narrated not by any human characters, but rather by a few famous gods and goddesses from Greek mythology. After being caught by her husband Hephaestus in an affair with a fellow god (Ares, god of war), Aphrodite, the goddess of l</span>
  <span id="freeText11645018807614699471" style="display:none">This was a delightful read, one that I was a bit apprehensive going into it, but ended up really enjoying! The premise of the story is a unique one: two young couples — Hazel and James, Colette and Aubrey — fall in love amongst the turbulence of World War I, their story narrated not by any human characters, but rather by a few famous gods and goddesses from Greek mythology. After being caught by her husband Hephaestus in an affair with a fellow god (Ares, god of war), Aphrodite, the goddess of love, seeks to avoid judgment on Mount Olympus by spinning the story of these 2 couples and the love that they share despite the world around them descending into chaos. But yet, this story isn’t just about love — it is also about the bonds of friendship and the unifying power of music, about courage in the face of adversity and destruction, about the possibility of hope after heartbreak, resilience after devastation. Ultimately, in a battle of Love versus War, will Love triumph or will War succeed in destroying everything in its path?<br /><br />This book is largely categorized as historical fiction, but at the same time, it can also be appropriately grouped under romance, YA, and fantasy. I will be honest in saying that, based on these genres, this is a book that I probably would not have picked up on my own to read due to the fact that, while I love historical fiction (and the author, Julie Berry, certainly did a great job with the historical elements in here – there were ample historical details but not to the point of dragging down the story), I’m not too keen on the other 3 genres. I don’t read much YA because I’m not the target audience for that genre and so I usually find it harder to appreciate the story and characters; with romance, I can be quite picky and usually don’t handle “overly sappy” stories well; and with fantasy, that’s just not really my thing. But given that this was the May selection for one of my book clubs, plus the story sounded interesting based on the summary and it came highly recommended by trusted friends, I decided to give this one a try and hope for the best. Well, this book ended up surprising me, but in a good way – all the genres blended together really well, the story was engaging, and the writing was lovely, but most important for me were the characters, all of whom I couldn’t help but love dearly. It’s not often that I feel like I don’t want a story to end because I want to keep reading about these characters and spend more time with them – this was definitely one of those instances!<br /><br />One thing that I think has to be mentioned, especially since the entire premise of the book hinges on this aspect, is the Greek mythology angle and the unique structure of having Aphrodite and the other gods narrate the main characters’ stories. From the various reviews, this aspect seemed to be a mixed bag in that it worked for some people but not for others. For me personally, it worked really well – in fact, I loved the cleverness of the way Berry structured the story, with having the appropriate god or goddess narrate the chapters based on their areas of expertise (for example – the chapters heavy on music were narrated by Apollo, the ones that revolved around the war battles were narrated by Ares, sections related to death or injury were narrated by Hades, and of course, the overall love story with the main characters was narrated by Aphrodite). Perhaps it is because I already had a certain familiarity with Greek mythology going into this, since I had studied it extensively back in my school days (albeit that was eons ago), so it helped me appreciate those aspects in a way that I probably would not have otherwise. With that said though, in terms of the sections where the gods (and goddess) interacted with each other, while I did find some of their banter funny, it got a bit old after a while, which made me somewhat impatient for them to get back to the actual story.<br /><br />The other thing that I felt this book did really well was balance – parts of the book were fun to read but the parts related to the war and its aftermath as well as other historical events were treated seriously as it needed to be. The story itself had substance, yet it wasn’t dense to the point of being overly complicated or hard to follow. This is one of those books that manages to blend the YA and adult aspects pretty well, without sacrificing the elements that also make this a worthwhile historical fiction read. Definitely recommended!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11645018807614699471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1153956735100461562" style="display:none">Julie Berry pens an utter delight in LOVELY WAR, an effervescent confection of a novel filled with humor, tragedy, romance, and myth. Four lovers meet in the chaos and terror of World War I--a shy English pianist, a gentle architect turned sharpshooter, a French singer scarred by German atrocities, and a brash musician bound for one of the all-African-American regiments heading overseas. Hovering over this love-struck war-bound quartet is the goddess of love herself, trying to ensure them happy endings in the midst of bloodshed, and fending off the impatient gods in her life who are more interested in death and war and revenge than love. Easily one of the best novels I have read all year!</span>

  <span id="freeText6602201779316034803" style="display:none">UPDATE: I haven't been able to find a playlist with the songs mentioned in this novel and since I loved it so much I decided to make my own:<a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/5AdARQkax9BqBSlx2AUcLM?si=qAjy-7w3SMufwiZ8hwoGUA" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify Link</a>. If you are currently reading this and stumble upon any songs I missed lmk!<br><br><b>
  <i>“Let them start their dreadful wars, let destruction rain down, and let plague sweep through, but I will still be here, doing my work, holding humankind together with love like this.”</i>
</b><br><br>Never in a million years would I have thought that a crossover between historical fiction and greek mythology would occur in a novel and have me feeling the way I feel. This novel is narrated through multiple Greek Gods, with the key narrator being Aphrodite. She narrates the story of two couples following them through WWI. She brilliantly interjects her narration with beautiful quotes like the one mentioned above. <br><br>The two couples that star in this story are so lovely and you instantly root for their happiness. Music, letters, and war all intertwine to fill your heart with romance and heartbreak. I would give anything to have a romantic stroll with my significant other in the heart of Paris. This novel had me crying on multiple occasions and it was impossible to put down. Sometimes all the war jargon was confusing, but I found it was necessary for the authenticity of the story. The final pages with historical notes from the author bring to light the harsh realities that took place that weren't fiction and give a good list of nonfiction recommended reads. <br><br>It's impossible for me to summarize just how much I loved this novel. I've been on the hunt for a romance novel and this exceeded any and all recommendations. I can't say enough how much I urge anyone I know to read this. I'm ending this review on a similar note as I always do:<br><blockquote>
  <i>Kisses by the billions happen every day, even in a lonely world like ours.<br>But this is a kiss for the ages.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594845935ra/29820264.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_2780556242" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2780556242" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52491901-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597005000p2/52491901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2780556242?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/52491901-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52491901-lena?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52491901-lena?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52491901-lena?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2780556242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5936945817415375803">A friend read this book before me and told me how much she loved it so I knew I had to get it, too. <br/><br/>Lovely War is a YA historical fiction novel set during World War I and told from the perspectives of various Greek gods, Aphrodite, the goddess of love, among them. The book focuses on two couples, Hazel & James, and Collette & Aubrey. <br/><br/>At a time where racism, prejudice and hatred were in full bloom, being black was tough. Aubrey Edwards himself is a young man from Harlem, talented Jazz musician an</span>
  <span id="freeText5936945817415375803" style="display:none">A friend read this book before me and told me how much she loved it so I knew I had to get it, too. <br /><br />Lovely War is a YA historical fiction novel set during World War I and told from the perspectives of various Greek gods, Aphrodite, the goddess of love, among them. The book focuses on two couples, Hazel &amp; James, and Collette &amp; Aubrey. <br /><br />At a time where racism, prejudice and hatred were in full bloom, being black was tough. Aubrey Edwards himself is a young man from Harlem, talented Jazz musician and so a member of the Army Band of the National Guard 15th New York Infantry Regiment (gosh I know that's a long name). Being shipped from one place to another, he never really gets to settle nor has time to think much about girls. As, one fateful day, the paths of young Aubrey and a talented orphan singer from Belgium cross, both are smitten with one another and thus, the story begins...<br /><br /><br />Hazel Windicott and James Alderidge, on the other hand, meet at a dance in London. Hazel is a talented piano player and dreamy young woman who catches the eye of James who dreams about one day becoming an engineer. Hazel, fully immersed in her playing the piano at first doesn't notice the glances James throws her way. But clever Aphrodite, who has been watching both of them intently for some time, can't help but give James a nudge. And so he asks her for a dance. A dance that will set things in motion neither one of them could've predicted...<br /><br />All of us know that war is never an easy, nor lovely thing. But the love in this book really is something special. All four stories of these young people captured my full attention from the start. The idea of Greek Gods telling such a story might seem absurd at first, but having read this book now it wasn't absurd at all. Reminiscent of the Book Thief in a way, this novel made my heart bleed and mended it at the same time. Reading about innocent young lives being thrown into an awful war was cruel and poignant, especially because a war leaves you scarred, but the book gives you hope. Hope that maybe one day, love can triumph over the century old hatred humans have been harvesting for one another and that the lives of a new generation should be preserved and cherished, not thrown away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5936945817415375803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2870440545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2870440545" />
    <a title="Katie Gallagher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79865972-katie-gallagher"><img alt="Katie Gallagher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557351146p2/79865972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2870440545?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Gallagher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Gallagher" href="/user/show/79865972-katie-gallagher">Katie Gallagher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2870440545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13361906967322090317"><i>
  <a href='https://katiejgallagher.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>For other fun bookish stuff, visit my blog!</a>
</i><br/><br/>This is one of those books with a cover that just called to me. (It’s also one of those covers embracing the <a href='https://katiejgallagher.com/2019/08/04/copycat-covers/' rel='nofollow noopener'>white-uppercase-sans-serif-with-stuff-over-it</a> trend.) But still, I went into <i>Lovely War</i> a bit trepidatious—I’m not the biggest historical fiction fan, and I spent a good portion of my time in school history classes daydreaming about being elsewhere.<br/><br/>Well, there was no reason to fear; this book swept me off my feet in a major way. I’d heard som</span>
  <span id="freeText13361906967322090317" style="display:none"><i>
  <a href="https://katiejgallagher.com" rel="nofollow noopener">For other fun bookish stuff, visit my blog!</a>
</i><br /><br />This is one of those books with a cover that just called to me. (It’s also one of those covers embracing the <a href="https://katiejgallagher.com/2019/08/04/copycat-covers/" rel="nofollow noopener">white-uppercase-sans-serif-with-stuff-over-it</a> trend.) But still, I went into <i>Lovely War</i> a bit trepidatious—I’m not the biggest historical fiction fan, and I spent a good portion of my time in school history classes daydreaming about being elsewhere.<br /><br />Well, there was no reason to fear; this book swept me off my feet in a major way. I’d heard some people be confused about the premise, and it is a bit odd, I’ll agree. The book starts off in World War Two times with Aphrodite—yes, <i>the</i> Aphrodite. She, along with some of her other friends from the Greek pantheon, narrates a gripping story from World War One about the intersection of love and war to her aggrieved husband, Hephaestus. He’s caught her cheating on him with Ares, and Aphrodite knows exactly the right tale to tell to explain the situation.<br /><br />I’ll admit that the Greek god framework does feel a little bit like the leaning tower of Pisa; it’s upright, but some tugging this way or that would cause the whole thing to topple over. <b>However</b>, the love story Aphrodite spins for Hephaestus and the readers is one for the ages. This is a captivating tale that literally moved me to tears, and that is a true once-in-a-blue-moon happening. Berry’s narration is gorgeous; quick chapters and lovable characters will have you make quick work of this 480-page tome.<br /><br />I’d argue that this is another case of “is it really YA?” (Hmm, sounds like an interesting game show.) It’s certainly being marketed in the YA section, and the tone is perfect for the YA crowd, but the main characters are older as far as I can tell. I’m not exactly sure what their ages were, to be honest—maybe it was mentioned, but I certainly missed it, so I’d guess they’re somewhere from eighteen to early twenties. (“<i>Maybe</i>,” hisses my inner conspiracy theorist, “Berry purposely didn’t mention the main characters’ ages so we can’t get into this whole debate again!”)<br /><br />Anyway, a good book is a good book, so maybe we should just get past the whole is-it-or-isn’t-it question. I wholeheartedly recommend <i>Lovely War</i>, and I dare you to read it without getting watery in the eyes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13361906967322090317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3236768768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6106793335168399565">I love the <i>idea</i> of this book. I love much of the execution of it too. But it just took too dang long to get anywhere. <br/>I get it. The tension builds as WW1 continues and the reader is left wondering what happened to the world's four most perfect lovebirds. Increasingly, though, I found myself wishing for more and more interruptions from the Greek gods. Those were funny, astute, and occasionally insightful moments. The romance itself was just sort of...<br/>* long sigh *<br/>Boring? <br/>Maybe I'm spoiled because</span>
  <span id="freeText6106793335168399565" style="display:none">I love the <i>idea</i> of this book. I love much of the execution of it too. But it just took too dang long to get anywhere. <br />I get it. The tension builds as WW1 continues and the reader is left wondering what happened to the world's four most perfect lovebirds. Increasingly, though, I found myself wishing for more and more interruptions from the Greek gods. Those were funny, astute, and occasionally insightful moments. The romance itself was just sort of...<br />* long sigh *<br />Boring? <br />Maybe I'm spoiled because I love my WW1 romances straight from the source (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/659784.Berta_Ruck" title="Berta Ruck" rel="nofollow noopener">Berta Ruck</a>) and I don't tend to read as much historical fiction these days. But it felt like a slog. <br />And yet I genuinely enjoyed many aspects of it. I totally want more of these Greek gods. And I would even take more Aphrodite inspired romances...just, with about 100 pages cut. Thanks.</span>

<div id="review_2734749120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2734749120" />
    <a title="Lindsay (pawsomereads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23203242-lindsay-pawsomereads"><img alt="Lindsay (pawsomereads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565655019p2/23203242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734749120?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay (pawsomereads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay (pawsomereads)" href="/user/show/23203242-lindsay-pawsomereads">Lindsay (pawsomereads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23203242-lindsay-pawsomereads?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734749120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13660535522372080016">I think I might be gushing about this book for the rest of my life.<br/>That being said, it’s almost too good I don’t even have the words to describe it, I loved everything about it. <br/>Beautiful is really the first word that comes to mind. The construction, the format, the writing, the plot, the characters; everything came together so perfectly. <br/>The whole premise of the book sounded so interesting to me and I absolutely love how all of the ideas in it were pulled together. Lovely War covers so many dif</span>
  <span id="freeText13660535522372080016" style="display:none">I think I might be gushing about this book for the rest of my life.<br />That being said, it’s almost too good I don’t even have the words to describe it, I loved everything about it. <br />Beautiful is really the first word that comes to mind. The construction, the format, the writing, the plot, the characters; everything came together so perfectly. <br />The whole premise of the book sounded so interesting to me and I absolutely love how all of the ideas in it were pulled together. Lovely War covers so many different things from war to romance to discrimination to mortality and it does so in such an exquisite manner. Each topic is covered in great detail without feeling like the book is trying to do too much. <br />The biggest thing that stood out to me at first was the writing itself. I adore the writing style. I can’t pinpoint exactly what it was about it that pulled me in so much but I feel like each character had such a distinct voice that were each captivating in their own way. I loved the descriptions and the overall flow of the novel as we follow the events across time. <br />The romance and relationships will completely pull at your heartstrings. These are deep and impactful connections that resonated so much as I was reading. I genuinely cared for all of these characters and their relationships and was so eager to see how things turned out for them. <br />The fact that this was told through the perspective of Greek gods made for such an interesting experience and I think that, while the love and war storylines were enough to stand on their own, the side trial of Aphrodite added the perfect extra layer. <br />If this book even sounds mildly interesting to you, I highly recommend giving it a try. It has easily become one of my new favorites of all time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13660535522372080016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10561578288411082266">Stunning. <br/><br/>Each of Julie's books is so different and so breathtaking. Here she presents dual stories: the Greek myth of Hephaestus capturing his wife Aphrodite with Ares, presented against the backdrop of WWII. But Aphrodite, as her defense, tells the story of star-crossed lovers she followed and aided during WWI. <br/><br/>Rich historical details about war, about the birth of jazz and ragtime, the clashing of cultures between the British, French, Belgian, and American allies, the first African American so</span>
  <span id="freeText10561578288411082266" style="display:none">Stunning. <br /><br />Each of Julie's books is so different and so breathtaking. But Aphrodite, as her defense, tells the story of star-crossed lovers she followed and aided during WWI. <br /><br />Rich historical details about war, about the birth of jazz and ragtime, the clashing of cultures between the British, French, Belgian, and American allies, the first African American soldiers . . . there's so much here! Julie has done her homework, and includes a lengthy author's note and a bibliography. </span>

<div id="review_2770537139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2770537139" />
    <a title="Morgan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54469541-morgan"><img alt="Morgan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566262460p2/54469541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2770537139?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/54469541-morgan">Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54469541-morgan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54469541-morgan?shelf=inspo-books">inspo-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54469541-morgan?shelf=read-do-not-own">read-do-not-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54469541-morgan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770537139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8254531010225643536">BRILLIANT!! ABSOLUTELY BRILLIANT!! There are a lot of books that I enjoy, and entertain me but there are <i>very</i> few that make me emotional on multiple different spectrums. The fact that <i>Lovely War</i> is the first book in years to make me cry, it easily became a favorite of mine and quite possibly the best book I have read this year. <br/><br/>Lovely War is genuinely one of the most heartwarming books you could pick up. Aphrodite claims that Love and War are eternally drawn to each other and she uses her fellow</span>
  <span id="freeText8254531010225643536" style="display:none">BRILLIANT!! ABSOLUTELY BRILLIANT!! There are a lot of books that I enjoy, and entertain me but there are <i>very</i> few that make me emotional on multiple different spectrums. The fact that <i>Lovely War</i> is the first book in years to make me cry, it easily became a favorite of mine and quite possibly the best book I have read this year. <br /><br />Lovely War is genuinely one of the most heartwarming books you could pick up. Aphrodite claims that Love and War are eternally drawn to each other and she uses her fellow Gods to support her claim. Throughout the story, we hear from Aphrodite (Love), Apollo (Music), Hades (Death), and Ares (War). Their narration is what made this story the gem it is. Our Gods share their appropriate stories of our main characters (Hazel, James, Aubrey, and Colette) journies through the first World War creating a cohesive and magical story that will be unlike anything else you have read before. <br /><br /><b>“The most ordinary mortal bodies are housed by spectacular souls”</b><br /><i>Hades, in my personal opinion, was the most articulate of the Gods, making me tear up more than I would care to admit.</i><br /><br />The characters will make you fall instantly in love with the story. Hazel and Colette have such a beautiful friendship and James and Aubrey are some of the finest gents you will come across in a book. Having four individually amazing characters supporting and pushing each other to improve was so refreshing I just <i>loved</i> it so much !!<br /><br />Julie Berry is a real Goddess who worked her magic on this book, her creation of the plot, the descriptions, the appropriate historical representations, etc. were all artfully done and my historical-fiction-loving-self ate this whole story up. I wish I could properly formulate my thoughts and put into words how charming and brilliant Lovely War is. Please do yourself a favor and go read Lovely War, you won’t regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8254531010225643536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3222555935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3222555935" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3222555935?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/46043207-lovely-war">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=romantic-recollections">romantic-recollections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=mythological-majesty">mythological-majesty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=historical-highness">historical-highness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222555935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12094987344748234268">Aphrodite is the goddess of love, and yet this is the one emotion she can not experience. Allure follows in her wake however, and none feels her pull more than Ares, the god of war. This inexplicable connection between love and war leads the great gods to stand trial for their coupling and Aphrodite calls upon mere mortals for her testimony. She shows how love and war will always thrive in the presence of the other, as two timeless world war love stories can attest to.<br/><br/>Historical romance is not m</span>
  <span id="freeText12094987344748234268" style="display:none">Aphrodite is the goddess of love, and yet this is the one emotion she can not experience. Allure follows in her wake however, and none feels her pull more than Ares, the god of war. This inexplicable connection between love and war leads the great gods to stand trial for their coupling and Aphrodite calls upon mere mortals for her testimony. She shows how love and war will always thrive in the presence of the other, as two timeless world war love stories can attest to.<br /><br />Historical romance is not my usual go-to genre and yet this unique mythological twist had me so intrigued! I adored how the gods formed a framework for this tale to be told inside of, and how their insertions into the story only served to highlight the emotion evident inside of it.<br /><br />Asides from the prevalent romance, this was also a horrifically tragic tale. Racism, PTSD, and the many other horrors of war featured throughout and these tougher issues provided a harsh juxtaposition for the sweet scenes of blossoming love to feature alongside. The presence of the two made this dually as harrowing as it was heart-warming and I thought the prevalent tragedies were sensitively delivered and necessary inclusions.<br /><br />The plot took many unforeseen twists and I never felt certain of the final destination this story would take the reader to. I adored how this concluded with a bittersweet authenticity that left me longing for me yet thoroughly satisfied with the character arcs and epic journeys my new favourites experienced.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12094987344748234268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28434314-brogan-lane?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28434314-brogan-lane?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3146508286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3679090388143657841">From page 1, I knew this book would be 5 stars. <br/><br/><b>How in the world have I only known about this book until this year? </b>It’s a crime! This is a stunning book! I have never felt such awe with a book like this one, and I don’t think I ever will again. Julie Berry’s writing is gorgeous and breath-taking. The intertwining lives of these four young people during the First World War was so beautifully crafted that I just wanted to cry all the time. I’ve mentioned in my reviews for <b>The Guernsey Literary an</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3679090388143657841" style="display:none">From page 1, I knew this book would be 5 stars. <br /><br /><b>How in the world have I only known about this book until this year? </b>It’s a crime! This is a stunning book! I have never felt such awe with a book like this one, and I don’t think I ever will again. Julie Berry’s writing is gorgeous and breath-taking. The intertwining lives of these four young people during the First World War was so beautifully crafted that I just wanted to cry all the time. I’ve mentioned in my reviews for <b>The Guernsey Literary and Potato Peel Pie Society by Annie Barrows and Mary Ann Shaffer</b> and <b>The Jane Austen Society by Natalie Jenner</b> that I avoid a lot of literature written/set during the World Wars, but I’ve been slowly dipping my toes into this genre. Yes, this book was about the war, but <b>Lovely War</b> is about love, peace, prejudice, grief, racism, death, mental illness, music, family, loss, friendship and THE GREEK GODS/GODDESSES! I bought this book specifically because the very concept of the Greek Gods/Goddesses narrating the lives of mortals during the war intrigued me so much! <br /><br />Holy crap was this a good book. I really can’t express my love for this book in words. I just really want to stand at the edge of the world and scream so loud my lungs hurt. <b>Lovely War is perfection</b> <br /><br /><b>”Let them start their dreadful wars, let destruction rain down, and let plague sweep through, but I will still be here, doing my work, holding humankind together with love like this.”</b> <br /><br />GIVE ME MORE OF JULIE BERRY’S BOOKS!!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770113449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13237556477457553092"><b>
  <i>”if music stops, and art ceases, and beauty fades, what have we then?”</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>second reread: april 26, 2020 - april 29, 2020</b><br/><br/>it’s been only a month and i’m already rereading this, which is shortest length between any rereads, love that for lovely war mwah. i adored this novel as much as i did the first time <3<br/><br/><br/><br/><b>first read: march 14, 2020 - march 19, 2020</b><br/><br/><i>lovely war</i> is one of my favorite stand alones. it provided me a new perspective on the costs of war. it was relatively lighthearted, though i’d put a <b>t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13237556477457553092" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”if music stops, and art ceases, and beauty fades, what have we then?”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>second reread: april 26, 2020 - april 29, 2020</b><br /><br />it’s been only a month and i’m already rereading this, which is shortest length between any rereads, love that for lovely war mwah. i adored this novel as much as i did the first time &lt;3<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>first read: march 14, 2020 - march 19, 2020</b><br /><br /><i>lovely war</i> is one of my favorite stand alones. it provided me a new perspective on the costs of war. it was relatively lighthearted, though i’d put a <b>trigger warning for attempted sexual assault</b>. i can’t explain why i love this story so much, but the immaculate story telling sure played a part. the fates of our four main characters (not counting aphrodite, hephaestus, hades, ares, and apollo) hazel, james, aubrey, and colette were beautifully woven together.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>”then be a monster,” she said. “do what you must to survive, so you can come back to me.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>”love and art go together like baritone and alto, paint and canvas, like sunrise and a burning atmosphere.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />the historical notes at the end were also of interest to me. from the 369th division and the wretched discrimination black people faced despite only wanting to prove they were as american as anyone else, to the long term effects on european and american women and the youth fighting the old generation’s war.<br /><br />having background knowledge from studying world war one in american and european history and reading <i>all quiet on the western front</i> by erich maria remarque, my experience reading this novel was enriched.<br /><br /><br /><i>lovely war</i> was, at the risk of me being redundant, a lovely story of love and heartbreak, art and music, injustice and sacrifice, life and death, and war and peace.<br /><br />i think a block of text from the historical context sums up my thoughts about this story.<br /><br /><i>”a frequent theme in the writings of men at the front was their marveling at how, over the shell-blasted wasteland of the killing fields, a glorious sunset could still paint the sky, or the freshness of dew and birdsong could still make morning sweet. even in the trenches <b>for all its horror and despair, for many, the great war sharpened life, showing it for the brief and fleeting gift it was, and revealing home, freedom, safety, family, beauty, and love to be precious beyond price.</b></i>”</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pB74MIJpS9ZgT+txBQ/Yn7ECAi/3jaGtJLV7+tvMlbYDp8oDVqYyBZDOvyZRve+Y7baDihpll3f5BomrLwI+Wg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
